{"parentUuid":"597fbf46-e8c3-475c-a68c-ecf7510174de","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"67fcde4a-7483-4526-a2da-9ae9514890c8","agentId":"ad849b8c0a7e95b8b","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_017bCFY5pccBoD3P9bApTDaC","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→name: wz:subagent-driven-development\n     3→description: Use when executing implementation plans with independent tasks in the current session\n     4→---\n     5→\n     6→# Subagent-Driven Development\n     7→\n     8→## Command Routing\n     9→Follow the Canonical Command Matrix in `hooks/routing-matrix.json`.\n    10→- Large commands (test runners, builds, diffs, dependency trees, linting) → context-mode tools\n    11→- Small commands (git status, ls, pwd, wazir CLI) → native Bash\n    12→- If context-mode unavailable, fall back to native Bash with warning\n    13→\n    14→## Codebase Exploration\n    15→1. Query `wazir index search-symbols <query>` first\n    16→2. Use `wazir recall file <path> --tier L1` for targeted reads\n    17→3. Fall back to direct file reads ONLY for files identified by index queries\n    18→4. Maximum 10 direct file reads without a justifying index query\n    19→5. If no index exists: `wazir index build && wazir index summarize --tier all`\n    20→\n    21→Execute plan by dispatching fresh subagent per task, with two-stage review after each: spec compliance review first, then code quality review.\n    22→\n    23→**Why subagents:** You delegate tasks to specialized agents with isolated context. By precisely crafting their instructions and context, you ensure they stay focused and succeed at their task. They should never inherit your session's context or history — you construct exactly what they need. This also preserves your own context for coordination work.\n    24→\n    25→**Core principle:** Fresh subagent per task + two-stage review (spec then quality) = high quality, fast iteration\n    26→\n    27→## When to Use\n    28→\n    29→```dot\n    30→digraph when_to_use {\n    31→    \"Have implementation plan?\" [shape=diamond];\n    32→    \"Tasks mostly independent?\" [shape=diamond];\n    33→    \"Stay in this session?\" [shape=diamond];\n    34→    \"subagent-driven-development\" [shape=box];\n    35→    \"executing-plans\" [shape=box];\n    36→    \"Manual execution or brainstorm first\" [shape=box];\n    37→\n    38→    \"Have implementation plan?\" -> \"Tasks mostly independent?\" [label=\"yes\"];\n    39→    \"Have implementation plan?\" -> \"Manual execution or brainstorm first\" [label=\"no\"];\n    40→    \"Tasks mostly independent?\" -> \"Stay in this session?\" [label=\"yes\"];\n    41→    \"Tasks mostly independent?\" -> \"Manual execution or brainstorm first\" [label=\"no - tightly coupled\"];\n    42→    \"Stay in this session?\" -> \"subagent-driven-development\" [label=\"yes\"];\n    43→    \"Stay in this session?\" -> \"executing-plans\" [label=\"no - parallel session\"];\n    44→}\n    45→```\n    46→\n    47→**vs. Executing Plans (parallel session):**\n    48→- Same session (no context switch)\n    49→- Fresh subagent per task (no context pollution)\n    50→- Two-stage review after each task: spec compliance first, then code quality\n    51→- Faster iteration (no human-in-loop between tasks)\n    52→\n    53→## The Process\n    54→\n    55→```dot\n    56→digraph process {\n    57→    rankdir=TB;\n    58→\n    59→    subgraph cluster_per_task {\n    60→        label=\"Per Task\";\n    61→        \"Capture PRE_TASK_SHA\" [shape=box];\n    62→        \"Dispatch implementer subagent (./implementer-prompt.md)\" [shape=box];\n    63→        \"Implementer subagent asks questions?\" [shape=diamond];\n    64→        \"Answer questions, provide context\" [shape=box];\n    65→        \"Implementer subagent implements, tests, commits, self-reviews\" [shape=box];\n    66→        \"Dispatch spec reviewer subagent (./spec-reviewer-prompt.md)\" [shape=box];\n    67→        \"Spec reviewer subagent confirms code matches spec?\" [shape=diamond];\n    68→        \"Implementer subagent fixes spec gaps\" [shape=box];\n    69→        \"Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent (./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md)\" [shape=box];\n    70→        \"Code quality reviewer subagent approves?\" implementer subagent commits before review. The spec reviewer and code quality reviewer must use `codex review --base <pre-task-sha>` to scope their review to the task's changes. Capture `PRE_TASK_SHA=$(git rev-parse HEAD)` before dispatching the implementer.\n   105→\n   106→### Review Loop Alignment\n   107→\n   108→Both review stages follow the review loop pattern in `docs/reference/review-loop-pattern.md` with explicit `--mode task-review`:\n   109→- **Spec compliance review:** Uses spec dimensions with `--mode task-review`\n   110→- **Code quality review:** Uses 5 task-execution dimensions with `--mode task-review`\n   111→\n   112→Review logs use task-scoped filenames: `execute-task-<NNN>-review-pass-<N>.md`\n   113→\n   114→Each review stage respects the loop cap via `wazir capture loop-check --task-id <NNN>`. If the cap is reached (exit 43), escalate to the controller (you) for a decision.\n   115→\n   116→### Codex Error Handling\n   117→\n   118→If codex exits non-zero during review, log the error, mark the pass as codex-unavailable, and use self-review findings only. Do not treat a Codex failure as a clean pass.\n   119→\n   120→**Standalone mode:** When no `.wazir/runs/latest/` exists, review logs go to `docs/plans/`.\n   121→\n   122→## Prompt Templates\n   123→\n   124→- `./implementer-prompt.md` - Dispatch implementer subagent\n   125→- `./spec-reviewer-prompt.md` - Dispatch spec compliance reviewer subagent\n   126→- `./code-quality-reviewer-prompt.md` - Dispatch code quality reviewer subagent\n   127→\n   128→## Advantages\n   129→\n   130→**vs. Manual execution:**\n   131→- Subagents follow TDD naturally\n   132→- Fresh context per task (no confusion)\n   133→- Parallel-safe (subagents don't interfere)\n   134→- Subagent can ask questions (before AND during work)\n   135→\n   136→**vs. Executing Plans:**\n   137→- Same session (no handoff)\n   138→- Continuous progress (no waiting)\n   139→- Review checkpoints automatic\n   140→\n   141→**Efficiency gains:**\n   142→- No file reading overhead (controller provides full text)\n   143→- Controller curates exactly what context is needed\n   144→- Subagent gets complete information upfront\n   145→- Questions surfaced before work begins (not after)\n   146→\n   147→**Quality gates:**\n   148→- Self-review catches issues before handoff\n   149→- Two-stage review: spec compliance, then code quality\n   150→- Review loops ensure fixes actually work\n   151→- Spec compliance prevents over/under-building\n   152→- Code quality ensures implementation is well-built\n   153→\n   154→**Cost:**\n   155→- More subagent invocations (implementer + 2 reviewers per task)\n   156→- Controller does more prep work (extracting all tasks upfront)\n   157→- Review loops add iterations\n   158→- But catches issues early (cheaper than debugging later)\n   159→\n   160→## Red Flags\n   161→\n   162→**Never:**\n   163→- Start implementation on main/master branch without explicit user consent\n   164→- Skip reviews (spec compliance OR code quality)\n   165→- Proceed with unfixed issues\n   166→- Dispatch multiple implementation subagents in parallel (conflicts)\n   167→- Make subagent read plan file (provide full text instead)\n   168→- Skip scene-setting context (subagent needs to understand where task fits)\n   169→- Ignore subagent questions (answer before letting them proceed)\n   170→- Accept \"close enough\" on spec compliance (spec reviewer found issues = not done)\n   171→- Skip review loops (reviewer found issues = implementer fixes = review again)\n   172→- Let implementer self-review replace actual review (both are needed)\n   173→- **Start code quality review before spec compliance is PASS** (wrong order)\n   174→- Move to next task while either review has open issues\n   175→- **Review the wrong diff -- always scope to the current task's changes using --base**\n   176→\n   177→**If subagent asks questions:**\n   178→- Answer clearly and completely\n   179→- Provide additional context if needed\n   180→- Don't rush them into implementation\n   181→\n   182→**If reviewer finds issues:**\n   183→- Implementer (same subagent) fixes them\n   184→- Reviewer reviews again\n   185→- Repeat until approved\n   186→- Don't skip the re-review\n   187→\n   188→**If subagent fails task:**\n   189→- Dispatch fix subagent with specific instructions\n   190→- Don't try to fix manually (context If no index exists: `wazir index build && wazir index summarize --tier all`\n    20→\n    21→Run the Clarifier phase — everything from reading input to having an approved execution plan.\n    22→\n    23→**Pacing rule:** This skill has mandatory user checkpoints between sub-workflows. Match scope tags against current run's intent (from run config `parsed_intent`) and detected stack (from research findings or `config.json` stack settings)\n    39→   4. Inject matching learnings into context, sorted by confidence (highest first), most recent first, limit 10\n    40→   5. Every wrong assumption here cascades into a wrong spec and wrong implementation.\n    65→>\n    66→> **Looking for:** Existing code patterns, dependency versions, external standard definitions, architectural constraints\n    67→\n    68→Delegate to the discover workflow (`workflows/discover.md`):\n    69→\n    70→1. **Keyword extraction:** Read the briefing and extract concepts/terms that are vague, reference external standards, or use unfamiliar terminology.\n    71→   - **When to research:** concept references an external standard by name, uses a tool/library not seen in the codebase, or is ambiguous enough that two agents could interpret it differently.\n    72→   - **When NOT to research:** concept is fully defined in the input, or it's a well-known programming concept.\n    73→2. **Fetch sources:** For each concept needing research:\n    74→   - Use `fetch_and_index` (if context-mode available) or `WebFetch` to fetch the source.\n    75→   - Save fetched content to `.wazir/runs/latest/sources/`.\n    76→   - Track each fetch in `sources/manifest.json`.\n    77→3. **Error handling:** 404/unreachable → log failure, continue. Research is best-effort.\n    78→4. The **researcher role** produces the research artifact.\n    79→5. The **reviewer role** runs the research-review loop with `--mode research-review`.\n    80→6. Loop runs for `pass_counts[depth]` passes.\n    81→\n    82→Save result to `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/research-brief.md`.\n    83→\n    84→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n    85→\n    86→> **Research complete.**\n    87→>\n    88→> **Found:** [N] external sources fetched, [N] codebase patterns identified, [N] architectural constraints documented\n    89→>\n    90→> **Without this phase:** Spec would be built on assumptions instead of evidence — wrong framework APIs, missed existing utilities, contradicted naming conventions\n    91→>\n    92→> **Changed because of this work:** [List of key discoveries — e.g., \"found existing auth middleware at src/middleware/auth.ts\", \"project uses Vitest not Jest\"]\n    93→\n    94→### Checkpoint: Research Review\n    95→\n    96→> **Research complete. Every ambiguity left here becomes a 50/50 coin flip during implementation that could produce the wrong feature.\n   118→>\n   119→> **Looking for:** Ambiguous requirements, implicit assumptions, missing constraints, scope boundaries, unresolved questions\n   120→\n   121→### Input Preservation (before producing clarification)\n   122→\n   123→1. If `.wazir/input/tasks/` is empty or missing, synthesize from `briefing.md` alone.\n   129→\n   130→### Informed Question Batching (after research, before producing clarification)\n   131→\n   132→Research has completed. Route feedback: plan corrections → `user-feedback.md`, new requirements → `briefing.md`.\n   199→\n   200→---\n   201→\n   202→## Sub-Workflow 3: Spec Harden (specify + spec-challenge workflows)\n   203→\n   204→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   205→\n   206→> **Spec Hardening** — About to convert the clarified scope into a measurable, testable specification and then run adversarial spec-challenge review to find gaps.\n   207→>\n   208→> **Why this matters:** Without hardening, acceptance criteria stay vague (\"it should work well\") instead of measurable (\"response time under 200ms for 95th percentile\"). This is where architectural mistakes get caught cheaply instead of discovered during implementation.\n   268→>\n   269→> **Looking for:** Architectural trade-offs, scalability implications, complexity vs. simplicity, alignment with existing codebase patterns\n   270→\n   271→Invoke the `brainstorming` skill (`wz:brainstorming`):\n   272→\n   273→1. Propose 2-3 viable approaches with explicit trade-offs\n   274→2. For each approach: effort estimate, risk assessment, what it enables/prevents\n   275→3. This is the most important checkpoint.\n   288→\n   289→Save approved design to `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/design.md`.\n   290→\n   291→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   292→\n   293→> **Brainstorming complete.**\n   294→>\n   295→> **Found:** [N] approaches evaluated, [N] trade-offs documented, [N] design-review findings resolved\n   296→>\n   297→> **Without this phase:** The first viable approach would be built without considering alternatives — potentially choosing a complex solution when a simple one exists, or an approach that conflicts with existing patterns\n   298→>\n   299→> **Changed because of this work:** [Selected approach and why, rejected alternatives and why, design-review adjustments made]\n   300→\n   301→After approval: design-review loop with `--mode design-review` (5 canonical dimensions: spec coverage, design-spec consistency, accessibility, visual consistency, exported-code fidelity).\n   302→\n   303→---\n   304→\n   305→## Sub-Workflow 5: Plan (plan + plan-review workflows)\n   306→\n   307→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   308→\n   309→> **Planning** — About to break the approved design into ordered, dependency-aware implementation tasks with a gap analysis against the original input.\n   310→>\n   311→> **Why this matters:** Without explicit planning, tasks get implemented in the wrong order (breaking dependencies), items from the input get silently dropped, and task granularity is either too coarse (monolithic changes that are hard to review) or too fine (overhead without value).\n   312→>\n   313→> **Looking for:** Correct dependency ordering, complete input coverage, appropriate task granularity, clear acceptance criteria per task\n   314→\n   315→Delegate to `wz:writing-plans`:\n   316→\n   317→1. Invoke `wz:reviewer --mode plan-review`.\n   319→3. Loop until clean or cap reached.\n   320→\n   321→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   322→\n   323→> **Planning complete.**\n   324→>\n   325→> **Found:** [N] tasks created, [N] dependencies mapped, [N] plan-review findings resolved, [N] gap analysis items addressed\n   326→>\n   327→> **Without this phase:** Tasks would be implemented in ad-hoc order breaking dependencies, input items would be silently dropped, and task sizes would vary wildly making review inconsistent\n   328→>\n   329→> **Changed because of this work:** [Task count, dependency chain summary, any items reordered or split during plan-review]\n   330→\n   331→### Checkpoint: Plan Review\n   332→\n   333→> **Implementation plan: [N] tasks**\n   334→>\n   335→> | # | Task | Complexity | Dependencies | Description |\n   336→> |---|------|-----------|--------------|-------------|\n   337→\n   338→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   339→- **Question:** \"Does the implementation plan look correct and complete?\"\n   340→- **Options:**\n   341→  1. \"Approved — ready for execution\" *(Recommended)*\n   342→  2. \"Reorder or split tasks\"\n   343→  3. \"Missing tasks\"\n   344→  4. \"Too granular / too coarse\"\n   345→\n   346→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   347→\n   348→---\n   349→\n   350→### Scope Coverage Gate (Hard Gate)\n   351→\n   352→Before presenting the plan to the user, verify ALL input items are covered:\n   353→\n   354→1. Count distinct items/deliverables in the input briefing (`.wazir/input/briefing.md` + any `input/*.md` files)\n   355→2. Count tasks in the execution plan\n   356→3. **If `tasks_in_plan < items_in_input`:** STOP and present:\n   357→\n   358→> **Scope reduction detected.** The input contains [N] items but the plan only covers [M].\n   359→>\n   360→> Missing items: [list]\n   361→\n   362→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   363→- **Question:** \"The plan is missing [N-M] items from your input. This is a hard rule.**\n   369→\n   370→Invariant: `items_in_plan >= items_in_input` unless user explicitly approves reduction.\n   371→\n   372→---\n   373→\n   374→## Reasoning Output\n   375→\n   376→Throughout the clarifier phase, produce reasoning at two layers:\n   377→\n   378→### User Output: Before Research\n   379→\n   380→```\n   381→I'm about to research your request. Here's what I need to figure out:\n   382→1. [specific thing] — because [why it matters for YOUR request]\n   383→2. [specific thing] — because [risk if we skip this]\n   384→3. [specific thing] — because [what could go wrong]\n   385→```\n   386→\n   387→### User Output: After Research\n   388→\n   389→```\n   390→Research complete. Here's what I found and why it matters:\n   391→1. [finding] — this means [impact on your project]\n   392→   Without this: [what would have gone wrong]\n   393→2. These aren't bureaucratic — each one prevents a specific mistake:\n   401→1. [question] — asking because [what goes wrong if I assume]\n   402→2. [question] — asking because [concrete risk]\n   403→```\n   404→\n   405→### User Output: Between Sub-Workflows\n   406→\n   407→```\n   408→[Previous workflow] complete. Moving to [next workflow] because [concrete reason].\n   409→Key input from previous step: [what carries forward and why it matters].\n   410→```\n   411→\n   412→**File (Layer 2):** Write `.wazir/runs/<id>/reasoning/phase-clarifier-reasoning.md` with structured entries per decision:\n   413→- **Trigger** — what prompted the decision\n   414→- **Options considered** — alternatives evaluated\n   415→- **Chosen** — selected option\n   416→- **Reasoning** — why\n   417→- **Confidence** — high/medium/low\n   418→- **Counterfactual** — what would go wrong without this info\n   419→\n   420→Examples of clarifier reasoning entries:\n   421→- \"Trigger: input says 'auth' without specifying provider. Options: ask user, assume OAuth2, assume magic links. Chosen: ask user. The host environment (Claude, Codex, Gemini, Cursor) remains the execution container. Wazir supplies the operating model, guardrails, and artifact contracts.\n     4→\n     5→## Core components\n     6→\n     7→| Component | Purpose |\n     8→|-----------|---------|\n     9→| Roles | Canonical contracts defining what each agent role does and produces |\n    10→| Workflows | Phase entrypoints that sequence roles through delivery |\n    11→| Skills | Reusable procedures (wz:tdd, wz:debugging, wz:verification, wz:brainstorming) |\n    12→| Hooks | Guardrails enforcing protected paths, loop caps, and capture routing |\n    13→| Expertise | 315 curated knowledge modules composed into agent prompts |\n    14→| Templates | Artifact templates for phase outputs and handoff |\n    15→| Schemas | Validation schemas for manifest, hooks, artifacts, and exports |\n    16→| Exports | Generated host packages tailored per supported host |\n    17→| Tooling | CLI for validation, indexing, recall, capture, and status |\n    18→\n    19→## Design influences\n    20→\n    21→| Source | What Wazir keeps |\n    22→|--------|----------------------|\n    23→| Wazir skill system | Disciplined workflows, TDD, verification, review rigor, skill ergonomics |\n    24→| Spec-Kit | Spec-first development, explicit artifacts, approval gates |\n    25→| Oh My Claude | Host-native prompt structure and operator ergonomics |\n    26→| autoresearch | Research loops, experiment tracking, self-improvement discipline |\n    27→\n    28→## Context and indexing\n    29→\n    30→Wazir ships a built-in local index and recall surface that reduces context window consumption by 60-80% on exploration-heavy phases.\n    31→\n    32→### Context tiers\n    33→\n    34→| Tier | Token budget | Content | When to use |\n    35→|------|-------------|---------|-------------|\n    36→| L0 | ~100 tokens | One-line identifier (name, kind, language, line range) | Inventory scans, deciding what to load |\n    37→| L1 | ~500-2k tokens | Structural summary (signature, fields, purpose, dependencies) | Understanding shape without full source |\n    38→| L2 | Full content | Exact line-bounded source slice | Implementation, debugging, code review |\n    39→\n    40→### Role-specific recall defaults\n    41→\n    42→Roles are assigned default tiers based on their information needs:\n    43→\n    44→- **Exploration roles** (clarifier, researcher, specifier, content-author, designer, planner) default to L1 -- they need to understand structure across many files without reading every line\n    45→- **Implementation roles** (executor, verifier) default to direct read (L2) -- they need exact source for code changes and verification\n    46→- **Review role** (reviewer) starts at L1 as a triage pass, escalating to direct read only for logic errors, security concerns, or ambiguous summaries\n    47→- **Learning role** (learner) defaults to L0 -- it needs only inventory-level context to identify what changed\n    48→\n    49→Every role includes a fallback chain: if the preferred tier fails (no index, no summaries), the role falls back to direct file reads. The system degrades gracefully -- no wasted tokens on failed index operations.\n    50→\n    51→### Capture routing\n    52→\n    53→Large tool output is routed to run-local files via `wazir capture route` and `wazir capture output`, keeping the context window lean. The agent receives a file path reference (~50 tokens) instead of the full output.\n    54→\n    55→### Pipeline integration points\n    56→\n    57→The index and recall surface integrates with the pipeline at five points:\n    58→\n    59→1. **Session start** -- the bootstrap hook runs `index refresh` (or `build` for first run) to ensure the index is current\n    60→2. **Scan project** -- the `scan-project` skill runs `index stats` to report index health in the project profile\n    61→3. **Debugging** -- the `wz:debugging` OBSERVE phase uses `index search-symbols` and `recall --tier L1` for symbol-first exploration\n    62→4. **Execute** -- the executor uses `recall file` and `recall symbol` for targeted source reads\n    63→5. **Verify** -- the verifier uses direct reads for full validation\n    64→\n    65→### Measuring savings\n    66→\n    67→`wazir capture usage` generates a per-run token savings report showing capture routing statistics and context window savings. This provides concrete evidence of token reduction per session.\n    68→\n    69→The context-mode integration remains an optional adapter -- off by default, never required for core install, build, or test paths.\n    70→\n    71→See [Indexing and Recall](indexing-and-recall.md) for full command details and extractor documentation.\n    72→\n    73→## Design Phase\n    74→\n    75→The design phase runs after specification and before planning. The `designer` role uses open-pencil MCP tools to produce visual designs from the approved spec. Outputs include a `.fig` design file, exported Tailwind JSX/HTML+CSS scaffolds, design tokens JSON, and screenshot PNGs.\n    76→\n    77→The `design-review` workflow validates designs against the spec before planning begins. The existing `review` workflow also checks design-vs-implementation alignment after execution.\n    78→\n    79→open-pencil is integrated as an optional adapter (`open_pencil`) — it is not required for core Wazir functionality.\n    80→\n    81→## Key references\n    82→\n    83→- [Roles & Workflows](roles-and-workflows.md)\n    84→- [Artifact Model](artifact-model.md)\n    85→- [Host Exports](../reference/host-exports.md)\n    86→- [Hooks](../reference/hooks.md)\n    87→- [Expertise & Antipatterns](composition-engine.md)\n    88→"}]},"uuid":"e40ff987-442c-4fe6-a85d-2bac8a2b657a","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:34:03.699Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"a89a0bdf-4a24-47a7-9522-e5ea8bdca85a","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

{"parentUuid":"e2a51318-a637-46ba-a78b-8a6a35567311","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"67fcde4a-7483-4526-a2da-9ae9514890c8","agentId":"ad849b8c0a7e95b8b","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01AmB5AhHNKM7gHGCbpanx8c","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Enforcement Research — 2026-03-20\n     2→\n     3→## The Answer\n     4→\n     5→**Prose instructions don't work. The agent will always rationalize skipping them.** Every framework that achieves reliable enforcement uses the same pattern: **the framework holds the loop, not the agent.**\n     6→\n     7→## The Three-Layer Strategy\n     8→\n     9→### Layer 1: Mechanical Hooks (agent CANNOT bypass)\n    10→\n    11→**Stop hook** blocks completion: `{\"decision\": \"block\", \"reason\": \"...\"}` — proven by ralph-loop plugin (official marketplace). The agent literally cannot stop until all artifacts exist.\n    12→\n    13→**PreToolUse hooks** block actions:\n    14→- `PreToolUse:Write|Edit` — blocks implementation code if no plan artifact exists\n    15→- `PreToolUse:Bash` — blocks `git commit` if no tests run, blocks `git push` if no review\n    16→- Returns `permissionDecision: \"deny\"` — the tool call is prevented entirely\n    17→\n    18→**State tracking** via `pipeline-state.json` — hooks READ state, CLI WRITES state. No race conditions.\n    19→\n    20→**Key: command hooks only, never prompt hooks.** Prompt hooks re-introduce the rationalization problem.\n    21→\n    22→### Layer 2: Subagent Isolation (agent CANNOT see full pipeline)\n    23→\n    24→From every framework (CrewAI, LangGraph, Symphony, ideation_team_skill): **give the agent a task, not a plan.**\n    25→\n    26→- Each phase is a separate subagent invocation\n    27→- Phase N+1 receives phase N's artifact as input — if it doesn't exist, the call fails\n    28→- The controller (wazir skill) holds the loop and decides what runs next\n    29→- No single agent can rationalize skipping from research to code\n    30→\n    31→### Layer 3: Persuasion Engineering (agent WON'T bypass — 72% compliance)\n    32→\n    33→From superpowers (100K stars, backed by Meincke et al. 2025, N=28,000):\n    34→\n    35→- **Rationalization tables** — enumerate exact thoughts the agent has when skipping, with rebuttals\n    36→- **\"Violating the letter is violating the spirit\"** — kills the #1 escape pattern\n    37→- **Red flags lists** — specific phrases that mean STOP\n    38→- **Authority + Commitment + Social Proof** — doubles compliance (33% → 72%)\n    39→- **CSO (Claude Search Optimization)** — skill descriptions must be triggers, never process summaries\n    40→\n    41→## Key Findings Per Source\n    42→\n    43→### Claude Code Hooks\n    44→- Stop hook CAN block (`{\"decision\": \"block\"}`) — proven by ralph-loop\n    45→- PreToolUse CAN deny AND modify tool calls — proven by context-mode plugin\n    46→- Hooks are stateless but can read/write files for state\n    47→- Hooks loaded at session start, can't be added mid-session\n    48→- **Limitation: hooks block actions but can't compel them**\n    49→\n    50→### Superpowers (100K stars)\n    51→- 100% prompt engineering, zero mechanical enforcement\n    52→- Single SessionStart hook injects meta-skill in `<EXTREMELY_IMPORTANT>` tags\n    53→- **Issue **CrewAI:** Python for-loop + guardrail functions. Agent produces output, framework validates.\n    60→- **LangGraph:** Channel triggers + NamedBarrierValue. Node can't fire until inputs ready.\n    61→- **Temporal:** `await` keyword is the enforcement. Language-level blocking.\n    62→- **Symphony:** State machine + data dependencies. Each phase produces data the next requires.\n    63→- **GitHub Actions:** `needs:` DAG. Scheduler prevents jobs from starting without dependencies.\n    64→- **Universal pattern:** framework holds program counter, not agent.\n    65→\n    66→### UX / User Engagement\n    67→- **bladnman/ideation_team_skill:** AskUserQuestion for pre-flight interview, depth-aware parameters, cognitive role separation across agents\n    68→- **Devin:** PR-as-proof, screen recordings, conversational Slack updates, async delegation\n    69→- **Copilot Workspace:** Spec → Plan → Code, each editable. Subagent-Per-Phase Architecture\n    84→\n    85→The `/wazir` skill becomes a CONTROLLER that:\n    86→- Spawns a clarifier subagent → receives clarification artifact\n    87→- Spawns a spec subagent → receives spec artifact\n    88→- Spawns a design subagent → receives design artifact\n    89→- Spawns an executor subagent → receives implementation\n    90→- Spawns a reviewer subagent → receives review verdict\n    91→- Each subagent sees ONLY its phase, not the full pipeline\n    92→\n    93→### 3. is not implementable\n    82→\n    83→The Augment tier assumed that placing a Wazir addendum at `~/.claude/skills/<skill-name>/SKILL.md` would layer Wazir context on top of the superpowers base skill. This assumption is wrong. **Skill shadowing is full-override, not merge/append.**\n    84→\n    85→### Evidence\n    86→\n    87→**1. `skills-core.js` `resolveSkillPath()` (superpowers v4.3.1)**\n    88→\n    89→The function at `lib/skills-core.js:108-140` checks personal skills directory first. If `~/.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` exists, it returns that file immediately and never reads the superpowers version. There is no content merging.\n    90→\n    91→```\n    92→// Try personal skills first (unless explicitly superpowers:)\n    93→if (!forceSuperpowers && personalDir) {\n    94→    const personalSkillFile = path.join(personalDir, actualSkillName, 'SKILL.md');\n    95→    if (fs.existsSync(personalSkillFile)) {\n    96→        return { skillFile: personalSkillFile, sourceType: 'personal', ... };\n    97→        // ^^^ returns here -- superpowers version never consulted\n    98→    }\n    99→}\n   100→```\n   101→\n   102→**2. Superpowers test suite confirms override behavior**\n   103→\n   104→`tests/opencode/test-skills-core.sh` line 336 asserts:\n   105→```\n   106→[PASS] Personal skills shadow superpowers skills\n   107→```\n   108→\n   109→The test creates `personal-skills/shared-skill/SKILL.md` and `superpowers-skills/shared-skill/SKILL.md`, resolves `shared-skill`, and verifies `sourceType` is `\"personal\"` -- the superpowers version is invisible.\n   110→\n   111→**3. Superpowers RELEASE-NOTES.md v3.3.0**\n   112→\n   113→Line 385 documents the behavior explicitly: \"Personal skills override superpowers skills when names match.\"\n   114→\n   115→**4. The `superpowers:` prefix bypass is not available in Claude Code**\n   116→\n   117→`skills-core.js` supports `superpowers:skill-name` syntax to force resolution to the superpowers version even when a personal skill shadows it. However, `skills-core.js` is only used by the OpenCode plugin (`/.opencode/plugins/superpowers.js`). Claude Code's native `Skill` tool has its own built-in resolution logic that does not expose this prefix bypass.\n   118→\n   119→### Alternatives Considered\n   120→\n   121→| Approach | Viable? | Why |\n   122→|---|---|---|\n   123→| Place addendum in `~/.claude/skills/<name>/` | No | Full override -- base skill content lost |\n   124→| Merge base + addendum in SKILL.md at install time | Partial | Would work but creates a maintenance coupling: every superpowers update requires re-merging. This is functionally identical to Own tier. |\n   125→| Inject Wazir context via CLAUDE.md | No | CLAUDE.md is project-scoped; skill behavior should be global across all projects |\n   126→| Use `superpowers:` prefix to load base, then append | No | Prefix only works in OpenCode's `skills-core.js`, not in Claude Code's native Skill tool |\n   127→| Propose upstream merge/append feature | Future | Would require a superpowers or Claude Code platform change |\n   128→\n   129→### Conclusion\n   130→\n   131→The Augment tier is architecturally impossible with the current skill discovery mechanism. All three former Augment skills (dispatching-parallel-agents, finishing-a-development-branch, using-git-worktrees) are reclassified to **Own** tier. Since the Wazir versions already carry the full superpowers base content plus Wazir additions, no content is lost -- the skills simply cannot delegate to a shared base.\n   132→\n   133→If superpowers or Claude Code introduces a composition/layering mechanism in the future (e.g., `extends: superpowers:dispatching-parallel-agents` in frontmatter), the Augment tier could be revisited.\n   134→\n   135→---\n   136→\n   137→## Observations\n   138→\n   139→1. **No Delegate candidates exist.** Every Wazir fork adds at minimum the Command Routing and Codebase Exploration preambles, which prevents pure delegation.\n   140→\n   141→2. **Augment tier is not implementable.** R2 validation (2026-03-19) found that skill shadowing in both superpowers `skills-core.js` and Claude Code's native Skill tool is full-override: placing a SKILL.md in `~/.claude/skills/<name>/` completely replaces the superpowers skill with the same name. There is no merge or append mechanism. The three former Augment candidates (dispatching-parallel-agents, finishing-a-development-branch, using-git-worktrees) have been reclassified to Own. See [Augment Mechanism](#augment-mechanism) for full analysis.\n   142→\n   143→3. **All 14 forked skills are Own** because either (a) they introduce structural process changes (review loops, pipeline mode, Codex integration, content restructuring) or (b) the Augment composition mechanism does not exist in the platform.\n   144→\n   145→4. **Token cost tradeoff is significant.** Several Wazir Own skills (tdd, verification, debugging, writing-skills) are dramatically shorter than their superpowers counterparts. The superpowers versions contain valuable rationalization prevention tables, detailed examples, and anti-pattern catalogs that enforce discipline. The Wazir versions trade this for token efficiency. This tradeoff should be revisited -- some of the removed discipline content may be worth recovering as separate reference files.\n   146→\n   147→5. **The `wz:` prefix is already applied** in skill names within the Wazir SKILL.md frontmatter for all forked skills, consistent with the Own tier convention.\n   148→"}]},"uuid":"40f3efb2-eff2-4e4d-9643-2d10d646b66c","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:34:43.526Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"02a442cf-f9e1-460e-ba0d-a744b3713666","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

input to having an implementation plan\n    19→- Includes: research, clarification, spec hardening, brainstorming/design, planning\n    20→- All review loops happen within this phase (research-review, clarification-review, spec-challenge, design-review, plan-review)\n    21→- Output: approved spec + design + execution plan with task specs\n    22→\n    23→### Phase 3: Executor\n    24→- The simplest phase — pure implementation\n    25→- Should work with a lower-quality model (e.g., Sonnet for executor, medium-quality for per-task reviewer)\n    26→- Per-task TDD cycle: write test → implement → review against task spec\n    27→- The per-task reviewer checks implementation against the TASK spec (not input)\n    28→- Should still produce the same quality results with cheaper models\n    29→\n    30→### Phase 4: Final Review\n    31→- Compare implementation against the ORIGINAL INPUT (not the task specs)\n    32→- The executor's per-task reviewer already validated against task specs — that's covered\n    33→- Final reviewer validates: does what we built actually match what the user asked for?\n    34→- Input-to-implementation comparison catches drift that task-level review misses\n    35→- After review: apply learnings (from the run)\n    36→- After review: prepare for next task (compress/archive unneeded files, write handoff)\n    37→- This is where learn + prepare-next phases get folded in\n    38→\n    39→### Key Principle\n    40→- Phase 3 executor reviewer reviews: implementation vs. task spec\n    41→- Phase 4 final reviewer reviews: implementation vs. original user input\n    42→- These are different concerns — task-level correctness vs. intent alignment\n    43→\n    44→### Online Research\n    45→- How MetaGPT structures its pipeline phases (ProductManager → Architect → Engineer → QA) — their phase boundaries and handoff contracts\n    46→- How OpenAI Symphony structures Poll → Dispatch → Resolve → Land — what happens between phases\n    47→- How CrewAI Flows handle phase transitions with routers and conditional branching\n    48→- How GitHub Spec-Kit structures spec → implement → verify — their phase model\n    49→- LangGraph's multi-step agent pipelines — how they define phase boundaries vs. node boundaries\n    50→- How Devin structures its planning → implementation → verification phases\n    51→- How Cursor Agent / Windsurf Cascade structure their internal pipeline phases\n    52→\n    53→---\n    54→\n    55→## 16. One-Command Install + Zero-Config Start\n    56→\n    57→**Goal:** Wazir should be one of the easiest agent frameworks to install and use.\n    58→\n    59→**Current experience (too many steps, one breaks):**\n    60→```bash\n    61→git clone wazir\n    62→npm install\n    63→npx wazir export build   # 4 host exports\n    64→npx wazir init            # interactive arrows — FAILS in Claude Code\n    65→# then learn phases, roles, skills, composition...\n    66→```\n    67→\n    68→**Target experience:**\n    69→```bash\n    70→npx wazir\n    71→```\n    72→\n    73→One command. Everything else is automatic or deferred until needed.\n    74→\n    75→**What `npx wazir` should do:**\n    76→1. Detect host (Claude Code? Codex? Cursor? Gemini?) from environment\n    77→2. Export the right files for that host automatically\n    78→3. Scan the project (language, framework, stack)\n    79→4. Ask \"What do you want to build?\" — one question, no config\n    80→5. Run the full pipeline\n    81→\n    82→**No init questions.** Defaults for everything:\n    83→- Depth: standard (override with `/wazir deep ...`)\n    84→- Intent: inferred from request text\n    85→- Teams: sequential (always)\n    86→- Model mode: detected from available tools\n    87→\n    88→**Install paths (from easiest to most control):**\n    89→\n    90→| Path | Command | Who |\n    91→|------|---------|-----|\n    92→| Plugin marketplace | `/plugin install wazir` | Claude Code users |\n    93→| npx (zero install) | `npx @wazir-dev/cli` | Any Node project |\n    94→| Global install | `npm i -g @wazir-dev/cli` | Power users |\n    95→| Clone + link | `git clone && npm link` | Contributors |\n    96→\n    97→**First-run experience:**\n    98→- No CLAUDE.md editing required\n    99→- No config files to create\n   100→- No concepts to learn upfront\n   101→- Just: install → `/wazir build me a login page` → pipeline runs\n   102→\n   103→**Deep when you need it:**\n   104→- `wazir config` for power users who want control\n   105→- `wazir doctor` to see what's configured\n   106→- `wazir stats` to see what Wazir saved you\n   107→- Expertise modules, review loops, composition — all there, all optional to understand\n   108→\n   109→**Principle:** Like git — `git init` is one command, `git config` is deep. Instant start, deep when you need it.\n   110→\n   111→### Online Research\n   112→- How superpowers plugin handles install (`/plugin marketplace add`) — onboarding flow, zero-config\n   113→- How Cursor rules / .cursorrules get auto-detected and applied — zero-config pattern\n   114→- How `create-react-app`, `create-next-app`, `create-t3-app` handle project scaffolding — one-command patterns\n   115→- How Vercel CLI (`npx vercel`) auto-detects framework and deploys — zero-config detection\n   116→- How `degit` (Rich Harris) handles instant project scaffolding without git history\n   117→- How Yeoman generators and `npm create` handle interactive scaffolding vs. zero-config\n   118→- How the Claude Code plugin marketplace install flow works (behind the scenes)\n   119→- How OpenAI Codex handles first-run experience — what config does it need?\n   120→- How aider (Paul Gauthier) handles zero-config start — `aider` just works in any repo\n   121→- How bolt.new / v0.dev handle instant project start with no config\n   122→\n   123→---\n   124→\n   125→## 15. SQLite State Database for Learnings, Findings, and Trends\n   126→\n   127→**What:** Extend the existing SQLite infrastructure (already used for index) with a `state.sqlite` for persistent cross-run data.\n   128→\n   129→**Why files don't work:** Can't query \"show me all executor learnings for node stack\", can't detect recurring findings, can't trend across runs without reading every past report.\n   130→\n   131→**New tables in `state.sqlite` (separate from `index.sqlite` to survive rebuilds):**\n   132→- `learnings` — id, source_run, category, scope_roles, scope_stacks, scope_concerns, confidence, recurrence_count, content, created_at, last_applied, expires_at\n   133→- `findings` — id, run_id, phase, source (internal/codex/self-audit), severity, description, resolved, finding_hash (for dedup/recurrence detection)\n   134→- `audit_history` — run_id, date, finding_count, fix_count, manual_count, quality_score_before, quality_score_after\n   135→- `usage_aggregate` — run_id, date, tokens_saved, bytes_avoided, savings_ratio, index_queries, routing_decisions\n   136→\n   137→**Key queries this enables:**\n   138→- `SELECT * FROM findings WHERE finding_hash IN (SELECT finding_hash FROM findings GROUP BY finding_hash HAVING COUNT(*) >= 2)` — recurring findings → auto-propose as learnings\n   139→- `SELECT run_id, finding_count FROM audit_history ORDER BY date` — trend tracking\n   140→- `SELECT * FROM learnings WHERE scope_stacks LIKE '%node%' AND confidence = 'high'` — targeted learning injection\n   141→- `SELECT SUM(tokens_saved) FROM usage_aggregate` — cumulative savings\n   142→\n   143→**No new dependency:** `node:sqlite` already used by the index. Same infrastructure, new file.\n   144→\n   145→### Online Research\n   146→- How CrewAI stores long-term memory (SQLite3 backend) — schema, query patterns, adaptive scoring\n   147→- How LangGraph Store uses PostgreSQL + pgvector for cross-session persistence — schema design\n   148→- How LangMem stores and retrieves memories with TTL and semantic search\n   149→- How Mem0 (formerly EmbedChain) structures its memory database — entities, relations, facts\n   150→- How OpenHands stores agent state and history across sessions\n   151→- SQLite FTS5 full-text search for finding content — already used by context-mode plugin\n   152→- How Datasette (Simon Willison) exposes SQLite as a browsable interface — could be useful for `wazir stats`\n   153→- How Litestream handles SQLite replication — relevant if state.sqlite needs backup/sync\n   154→- SQLite WAL mode for concurrent reads during pipeline execution\n   155→\n   156→---\n   157→\n   158→## 14. Self-Audit V2 — Learnings + Trend Tracking + Severity\n   159→\n   160→**What:** Current self-audit finds and fixes issues but doesn't learn from them. Needs a second pass.\n   161→\n   162→**What's missing:**\n   163→\n   164→1. **No learning** — findings should feed into `memory/learnings/proposed/`. If the same issue recurs across audits, it becomes an accepted learning injected into executor context to prevent the issue from being created.\n   165→\n   166→2. **No comparison to previous audits** — each audit starts fresh with no awareness of what was found last time. Should track: \"last audit found 12 issues, this time 8 — are they the same or new?\" Trend detection across runs.\n   167→\n   168→3. **Fixes are mechanical only** — can fix lint, stale exports, broken references. Can't fix architectural drift, skill degradation, logic issues. These become \"manual required\" that nobody acts on. Need: escalation path for manual findings (create a task? file an issue?).\n   169→\n   170→4. **No severity or prioritization** — all findings are equal. Should have severity levels: critical (abort loop), high (fix now), medium (fix if time), low (log and skip).\n   171→\n   172→5. **Doesn't audit its own effectiveness** — after 5 loops, did the fixes improve anything? Need a before/after quality score per loop to measure convergence quality, not just convergence count.\n   173→\n   174→**Connection to item #13:** Self-audit findings should feed the SAME learning pipeline as review findings. Both are signals about recurring quality issues.\n   175→\n   176→### Online Research\n   177→- How SonarQube tracks code quality trends across builds — severity levels, technical debt measurement\n   178→- How CodeClimate maintains quality scores over time — GPA model, trend detection\n   179→- How GitHub Advanced Security tracks recurring vulnerabilities — alert lifecycle (open → dismissed → fixed → reopened)\n   180→- How ESLint's `--cache` tracks which files have been linted before — incremental audit pattern\n   181→- How Snyk tracks dependency vulnerabilities across versions — recurring vs. new findings\n   182→- How PagerDuty/OpsGenie handle alert fatigue and dedup — relevant for finding dedup\n   183→- How Netflix Chaos Monkey evolved its audit approach — game days, severity escalation\n   184→- Academic: \"Technical Debt Detection and Management\" survey papers — automated detection patterns\n   185→\n   186→---\n   187→\n   188→## 13. Internal Review First, Codex Second + Review Findings Feed Learning\n   189→\n   190→**What:** Restructure the review loop: internal review skill first (fast, cheap, expertise-loaded), Codex second (slow, expensive, fresh eyes). Review findings must feed the learning system.\n   191→\n   192→**Current problem:**\n   193→- Everything goes to Codex first — slow, expensive, overkill for most findings\n   194→- Review findings are consumed and forgotten — same mistakes repeat across runs\n   195→- Wazir is not evolving from its own reviews\n   196→\n   197→**New review flow:**\n   198→1. **Internal review** — `wz:reviewer` with full expertise modules composed in context (composition engine). Catches ~80% of issues. Uses Sonnet (not Opus). Fast and cheap.\n   199→2. **Fix cycle** — executor fixes internal findings, re-review internally until clean\n   200→3. **Codex review** — only AFTER internal review passes. Fresh eyes on clean code. Catches subtle issues the internal reviewer missed.\n   201→4. **Fix cycle** — executor fixes Codex findings\n   202→5. **Learning extraction** — ALL review findings (internal + Codex) feed into the learning system\n   203→\n   204→**Review findings → Learning pipeline:**\n   205→- After each run, the learner role scans all review findings\n   206→- Findings that recur across 2+ runs → auto-proposed as learnings\n   207→- Recurring learnings get injected into future executor context\n   208→- Example: if Codex keeps finding \"missing error handling in async functions\" across 3 runs, that becomes an accepted learning injected into every future executor prompt\n   209→- This is how Wazir evolves — it stops making the same mistakes\n   210→\n   211→**Reference skills:**\n   212→- superpowers: `requesting-code-review` (dispatches review subagent)\n   213→- CodeRabbit: `code-reviewer` (autonomous review agent)\n   214→- Wazir: `wz:reviewer` (phase-aware, multi-mode)\n   215→\n   216→**Decision needed:** Should internal review use a dedicated review subagent (like superpowers) or the current inline reviewer skill?\n   217→\n   218→### Online Research\n   219→- How superpowers `requesting-code-review` dispatches review subagents — architecture and prompt design\n   220→- How CodeRabbit AI review agent works — what it checks, how it structures findings\n   221→- How GitHub Copilot code review works — inline suggestions vs. PR-level review\n   222→- How Amazon CodeGuru Reviewer detects recurring patterns — ML-based finding detection\n   223→- How Google's Critique (internal code review tool) prioritizes findings\n   224→- How Facebook/Meta's Sapienz handles automated test generation from review findings\n   225→- How Sourcery.ai structures automated code review — rules vs. AI vs. hybrid\n   226→- How Qodo (formerly CodiumAI) generates review-driven test suggestions\n   227→- LangMem's prompt optimization from feedback — how review findings become prompt improvements\n   228→- Academic: \"Learning from Code Reviews\" — mining patterns from historical review data\n   229→\n   230→---\n   231→\n   232→## 12. Opus Orchestrator with Model-Aware Delegation\n   233→\n   234→**What:** Opus acts as orchestrator and decides which model handles each sub-task. Not \"Phase 3 uses Sonnet\" — every sub-task across all phases gets the cheapest model that can do it.\n   235→\n   236→**Examples:**\n   237→| Sub-task | Model | Why |\n   238→|----------|-------|-----|\n   239→| Orchestration / decisions | Opus | Needs judgment |\n   240→| Fetch URL content | Haiku | Mechanical, no reasoning |\n   241→| Read/summarize a file | Sonnet | Comprehension, not deep reasoning |\n   242→| Write implementation code | Sonnet | Good spec + plan = mechanical |\n   243→| Per-task code review | Sonnet | Diff review against clear spec |\n   244→| Spec hardening / design | Opus | Creativity + adversarial thinking |\n   245→| Final review (input vs impl) | Opus | Holistic judgment |\n   246→| Apply learnings | Sonnet | Structured extraction |\n   247→| Write handoff / compress | Haiku | Mechanical file operations |\n   248→\n   249→**How:** Claude Code supports `model` field in agent frontmatter (`model: sonnet | opus | haiku | inherit`). Opus spawns subagents with explicit model overrides via the Agent tool.\n   250→\n   251→**What needs to change:**\n   252→- Implement the `multi-model` mode in config (exists as option, never built)\n   253→- Add model-routing logic: Opus decides model per sub-task based on task complexity\n   254→- Composition engine dispatch includes model selection\n   255→- Skills/workflows annotate which sub-tasks are Haiku/Sonnet/Opus-grade\n   256→\n   257→**Principle:** Not all clarifier sub-agents should be Opus. The agent that grabs data from the internet doesn't need Opus. The one that designs the architecture does.\n   258→\n   259→### Online Research\n   260→- How BAMAS (Budget-Aware Multi-Agent Structuring) models cost budgets in multi-agent systems — academic paper\n   261→- How AutoGen/AG2 handles model routing across agent roles — model selection per agent\n   262→- How CrewAI assigns different LLMs to different agents — per-agent model configuration\n   263→- How LangGraph routes to different models based on task complexity — conditional model selection\n   264→- How OpenRouter handles model routing and fallback — API-level model selection patterns\n   265→- How Anthropic's own Claude Agent SDK handles model selection for subagents\n   266→- How Martian's model router selects optimal model per query — automated model routing\n   267→- Token cost comparison across models (Opus vs Sonnet vs Haiku) for different task types\n   268→- How the Mixture of Agents (MoA) pattern uses cheap models for drafting, expensive for refinement\n   269→\n   270→---\n   271→\n   272→## 11. Phase Reports Still Partially Prose-Based\n   273→\n   274→**What:** The reviewer skill has instructions to generate phase reports per the new schema, but there's no executable code that auto-generates the JSON. {"parentUuid":"ce7d207a-4067-40e4-8dfb-f44a55898a6d","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"67fcde4a-7483-4526-a2da-9ae9514890c8","agentId":"ad849b8c0a7e95b8b","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_012c2C6u6sZ1KquxprjyknEp","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→name: wz:wazir\n     3→description: One-command pipeline — type /wazir followed by what you want to build. Handles init, clarification, execution, review, and audits automatically.\n     4→---\n     5→\n     6→# Wazir — Full Pipeline Runner\n     7→\n     8→The user typed `/wazir <their request>`. Run the entire pipeline end-to-end, handling each phase automatically and only pausing where human input is required.\n     9→\n    10→All questions use **numbered interactive options** — one question at a time, defaults marked \"(Recommended)\", wait for user response before proceeding.\n    11→\n    12→## User Input Capture\n    13→\n    14→After every user response (approval, correction, rejection, redirect, instruction), capture it:\n    15→\n    16→```\n    17→captureUserInput(runDir, { phase: '<current-phase>', type: '<instruction|approval|correction|rejection|redirect>', content: '<user message>', context: '<what prompted the question>' })\n    18→```\n    19→\n    20→This uses `tooling/src/capture/user-input.js`. The log at `user-input-log.ndjson` feeds the learning system — user corrections are the strongest signal for improvement. At run end, prune logs older than 10 runs via `pruneOldInputLogs(stateRoot, 10)`.\n    21→\n    22→## Command Routing\n    23→Follow the Canonical Command Matrix in `hooks/routing-matrix.json`.\n    24→- Large commands (test runners, builds, diffs, dependency trees, linting) → context-mode tools\n    25→- Small commands (git status, ls, pwd, wazir CLI) → native Bash\n    26→- If context-mode unavailable, fall back to native Bash with warning\n    27→\n    28→## Codebase Exploration\n    29→1. Query `wazir index search-symbols <query>` first\n    30→2. Use `wazir recall file <path> --tier L1` for targeted reads\n    31→3. Fall back to direct file reads ONLY for files identified by index queries\n    32→4. Maximum 10 direct file reads without a justifying index query\n    33→5. If no index exists: `wazir index build && wazir index summarize --tier all`\n    34→\n    35→## Subcommand Detection\n    36→\n    37→Before anything else, check if the request starts with a known subcommand:\n    38→\n    39→| Input | Action |\n    40→|-------|--------|\n    41→| `/wazir audit ...` | Jump to **Audit Mode** (see below) |\n    42→| `/wazir prd [run-id]` | Jump to **PRD Mode** (see below) |\n    43→| `/wazir init` | Invoke the `init-pipeline` skill directly, then stop |\n    44→| Anything else | Continue to Phase 1 (Init) |\n    45→\n    46→---\n    47→\n    48→# 4-Phase Pipeline\n    49→\n    50→The pipeline has 4 phases. Each phase groups related workflows. Individual workflows within a phase can be enabled/disabled via `workflow_policy` in run-config.\n    51→\n    52→| Phase | Contains | Owner Skill | Key Output |\n    53→|-------|----------|-------------|------------|\n    54→| **Init** | Setup, prereqs, run directory, input scan | `wz:wazir` (inline) | `run-config.yaml` |\n    55→| **Clarifier** | Research, clarify, specify, brainstorm, plan | `wz:clarifier` | Approved spec + design + plan |\n    56→| **Executor** | Implement, verify | `wz:executor` | Code + verification proof |\n    57→| **Final Review** | Review vs original input, learn, prepare next | `wz:reviewer` | Verdict + learnings + handoff |\n    58→\n    59→---\n    60→\n    61→# Phase 1: Init\n    62→\n    63→## Step 1: Capture the Request\n    64→\n    65→Take whatever the user wrote after `/wazir` and save it as the briefing:\n    66→\n    67→1. Create `.wazir/input/` if it doesn't exist\n    68→2. Write the user's request to `.wazir/input/briefing.md` with a timestamp header\n    69→\n    70→If the user provided no text after `/wazir`, ask:\n    71→\n    72→> **What would you like to build?**\n    73→\n    74→Save their answer as the briefing, then continue.\n    75→\n    76→### Scan Input Directory\n    77→\n    78→Scan both `input/` (project-level) and `.wazir/input/` (state-level) for existing briefing materials. If files exist beyond `briefing.md`, list them:\n    79→\n    80→> **Found input files:**\n    81→> - `input/2026-03-19-deferred-items.md`\n    82→> - `.wazir/input/briefing.md`\n    83→>\n    84→> Using all found input as context for clarification.\n    85→\n    86→### Inline Modifiers\n    87→\n    88→Parse the request for inline modifiers before the main text:\n    89→\n    90→- `/wazir quick fix the login redirect` → depth = quick, intent = bugfix\n    91→- `/wazir deep design a new onboarding flow` → depth = deep, intent = feature\n    92→\n    93→Recognized modifiers:\n    94→- **Depth:** `quick`, `deep` (standard is default when omitted)\n    95→- **Interaction mode:** `auto`, `interactive` (guided is default when omitted)\n    96→  - `/wazir auto fix the auth bug` → interaction_mode = auto\n    97→  - `/wazir interactive design the onboarding` → interaction_mode = interactive\n    98→- **Intent:** `bugfix`, `feature`, `refactor`, `docs`, `spike`\n    99→\n   100→## Step 2: Check Prerequisites\n   101→\n   102→### CLI Check\n   103→\n   104→Run `which wazir` to check if the CLI is installed.\n   105→\n   106→**If not installed**, present:\n   107→\n   108→> **The Wazir CLI is not installed. It's required for event capture, validation, and indexing.**\n   109→\n   110→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   111→- **Question:** \"The Wazir CLI is not installed. How would you like to install it?\"\n   112→- **Options:**\n   113→  1. \"npm install -g @wazir-dev/cli\" *(Recommended)*\n   114→  2. \"npm link from the Wazir project root\"\n   115→\n   116→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   117→\n   118→The CLI is **required** — the pipeline uses `wazir capture`, `wazir validate`, `wazir index`, and `wazir doctor` throughout execution.\n   119→\n   120→**If installed**, run `wazir doctor --json` to verify repo health. Stop if unhealthy.\n   121→\n   122→### Branch Check\n   123→\n   124→Run `wazir validate branches` to check the current git branch.\n   125→\n   126→- If on `main` or `develop`:\n   127→  > You're on **[branch]**. The pipeline requires a feature branch.\n   128→\n   129→  Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   130→  - **Question:** \"You're on a protected branch. Create a feature branch?\"\n   131→  - **Options:**\n   132→    1. \"Create feat/<slug> from current branch\" *(Recommended)*\n   133→    2. \"Continue on current branch — not recommended\"\n   134→\n   135→  Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   136→\n   137→### Index Check\n   138→\n   139→```bash\n   140→INDEX_STATS=$(wazir index stats --json 2>/dev/null)\n   141→FILE_COUNT=$(echo \"$INDEX_STATS\" | jq -r '.file_count // 0')\n   142→if [ \"$FILE_COUNT\" -eq 0 ]; then\n   143→  wazir index build && wazir index summarize --tier all\n   144→else\n   145→  wazir index refresh\n   146→fi\n   147→```\n   148→\n   149→### Pipeline Init Check\n   150→\n   151→Check if `.wazir/state/config.json` exists.\n   152→\n   153→- **If missing** — invoke the `init-pipeline` skill.\n   154→- **If exists** — continue.\n   155→\n   156→## Step 3: Create Run Directory\n   157→\n   158→Generate a run ID using the current timestamp: `run-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS`\n   159→\n   160→```bash\n   161→mkdir -p .wazir/runs/run-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS/{sources,tasks,artifacts,reviews,clarified}\n   162→ln -sfn run-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS .wazir/runs/latest\n   163→```\n   164→\n   165→Initialize event capture:\n   166→\n   167→```bash\n   168→wazir capture init --run <run-id> --phase init --status starting\n   169→```\n   170→\n   171→### Resume Detection\n   172→\n   173→Check if a previous incomplete run exists (via `latest` symlink pointing to a run without `completed_at`).\n   174→\n   175→**If previous incomplete run found**, present:\n   176→\n   177→> **A previous incomplete run was detected:** `<previous-run-id>`\n   178→\n   179→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   180→- **Question:** \"A previous incomplete run was detected. Resume or start fresh?\"\n   181→- **Options:**\n   182→  1. \"Resume from the last completed phase\" *(Recommended)*\n   183→  2. \"Start fresh with a new empty run\"\n   184→\n   185→Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   186→\n   187→**If Resume:**\n   188→- Copy `clarified/` from previous run into new run, EXCEPT `user-feedback.md`.\n   189→- Detect last completed phase by checking which artifacts exist.\n   190→- **Staleness check:** If input files are newer than copied artifacts, warn and offer to re-run clarification.\n   191→\n   192→## Step 4: Build Run Config\n   193→\n   194→**No questions asked.** Depth, intent, and mode are all inferred or defaulted.\n   195→\n   196→### Intent Inference\n   197→\n   198→Infer intent from the request text using keyword matching:\n   199→\n   200→| Keywords in request | Inferred Intent |\n   201→|-------------------|-----------------|\n   202→| fix, bug, broken, crash, error, issue, wrong | `bugfix` |\n   203→| refactor, clean, restructure, reorganize, rename, simplify | `refactor` |\n   204→| doc, document, readme, guide, explain | `docs` |\n   205→| research, spike, explore, investigate, prototype | `spike` |\n   206→| (anything else) | `feature` |\n   207→\n   208→Depth defaults to `standard`. Override only via inline modifiers (`/wazir quick ...`, `/wazir deep ...`).\n   209→\n   210→### Write Run Config\n   211→\n   212→Save to `.wazir/runs/<run-id>/run-config.yaml`:\n   213→\n   214→```yaml\n   215→run_id: run-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS\n   216→parent_run_id: null\n   217→continuation_reason: null\n   218→\n   219→request: \"the original user request\"\n   220→request_summary: \"short summary\"\n   221→parsed_intent: feature\n   222→entry_point: \"/wazir\"\n   223→\n   224→depth: standard\n   225→interaction_mode: guided  # auto | guided | interactive\n   226→\n   227→# Workflow policy — individual workflows within each phase\n   228→workflow_policy:\n   229→  # Clarifier phase workflows\n   230→  discover:       { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   231→  clarify:        { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   232→  specify:        { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   233→  spec-challenge: { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   234→  author:         { enabled: false, loop_cap: 10 }\n   235→  design:         { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   236→  design-review:  { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   237→  plan:           { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   238→  plan-review:    { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   239→  # Executor phase workflows\n   240→  execute:        { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   241→  verify:         { enabled: true, loop_cap: 5 }\n   242→  # Final Review phase workflows\n   243→  review:         { enabled: true, loop_cap: 10 }\n   244→  learn:          { enabled: true, loop_cap: 5 }\n   245→  prepare_next:   { enabled: true, loop_cap: 5 }\n   246→  run_audit:      { enabled: false, loop_cap: 10 }\n   247→\n   248→research_topics: []\n   249→\n   250→created_at: \"YYYY-MM-DDTHH:MM:SSZ\"\n   251→completed_at: null\n   252→```\n   253→\n   254→### Workflow Skip Rules\n   255→\n   256→Map intent + depth to applicable workflows. The system decides — the user does NOT pick.\n   257→\n   258→| Class | Workflows | Rules |\n   259→|-------|-----------|-------|\n   260→| **Core** (always run) | `clarify`, `execute`, `verify`, `review` | Never skipped |\n   261→| **Adaptive** (run when evidence says so) | `discover`, `design`, `author`, `specify` | Skipped for bugfix/docs/spike at quick depth |\n   262→| **Scale** (intensity varies) | `spec-challenge`, `plan-review`, `design-review` | Loop cap controls iteration depth |\n   263→| **Post-run** (always run) | `learn`, `prepare_next` | Part of Final Review phase |\n   264→\n   265→Log skip decisions with reasons in `workflow_policy`.\n   266→\n   267→### Confidence Gate\n   268→\n   269→After building run config:\n   270→\n   271→- **High confidence** — one-line summary and proceed:\n   272→  > **Running: standard depth, feature, sequential. Proceeding...**\n   273→\n   274→- **Low confidence** — show plan and ask:\n   275→\n   276→  Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   277→  - **Question:** \"Does this run configuration look right?\"\n   278→  - **Options:**\n   279→    1. \"Yes, proceed\" *(Recommended)*\n   280→    2. \"No, let me adjust\"\n   281→\n   282→  Wait for the user's selection before continuing.\n   283→\n   284→```bash\n   285→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_exit --phase init --status completed\n   286→```\n   287→\n   288→Run the phase report and display it to the user:\n   289→```bash\n   290→wazir report phase --run <run-id> --phase init\n   291→```\n   292→\n   293→Output the report content to the user in the conversation.\n   294→\n   295→---\n   296→\n   297→# Interaction Modes\n   298→\n   299→The `interaction_mode` field in run-config controls how the pipeline interacts with the user:\n   300→\n   301→| Mode | Inline modifier | Behavior | Best for |\n   302→|------|----------------|----------|----------|\n   303→| **`guided`** | (default) | Pipeline runs, pauses at phase checkpoints for user approval. Current default behavior. | Most work |\n   304→| **`auto`** | `/wazir auto ...` | No human checkpoints. Codex reviews all. Gating agent decides continue/loop_back/escalate. Stops ONLY on escalate. | Overnight, clear spec, well-understood domain |\n   305→| **`interactive`** | `/wazir interactive ...` | More questions, more discussion, co-designs with user. Researcher presents options. Executor checks approach before coding. | Ambiguous requirements, new domain, learning |\n   306→\n   307→## `auto` mode constraints\n   308→\n   309→- **Codex REQUIRED** — refuse to start auto mode if `multi_tool.codex` is not configured in `.wazir/state/config.json`. Error: \"Auto mode requires an external reviewer (Codex). Configure it first or use guided mode.\"\n   310→- **On escalate:** STOP immediately, write the escalation reason to `.wazir/runs/<id>/escalations/`, and wait for user input\n   311→- **Wall-clock limit:** default 4 hours. If exceeded, stop with escalation.\n   312→- **Never auto-commits to main** — always work on feature branch\n   313→- All checkpoints (AskUserQuestion) are skipped — gating agent evaluates phase reports and decides\n   314→\n   315→## `guided` mode (default)\n   316→\n   317→Current behavior — no changes needed. Checkpoints at phase boundaries, user approves before advancing.\n   318→\n   319→## `interactive` mode\n   320→\n   321→- **Clarifier:** asks more detailed questions, presents research findings with options: \"I found 3 approaches — which interests you?\"\n   322→- **Executor:** checks approach before coding: \"I'm about to implement auth with Supabase — sound right?\"\n   323→- **Reviewer:** discusses findings with user, not just presents verdict: \"I found a potential auth bypass — here's why I think it's high severity, do you agree?\"\n   324→- Slower but highest quality for complex/ambiguous work\n   325→\n   326→## Mode checking in phase skills\n   327→\n   328→All phase skills check `interaction_mode` from run-config at every checkpoint:\n   329→\n   330→```\n   331→# Read from run-config\n   332→interaction_mode = run_config.interaction_mode ?? 'guided'\n   333→\n   334→# At each checkpoint:\n   335→if interaction_mode == 'auto':\n   336→    # Skip checkpoint, let gating agent decide\n   337→elif interaction_mode == 'interactive':\n   338→    # More detailed question, present options, discuss\n   339→else:\n   340→    # guided — standard checkpoint with AskUserQuestion\n   341→```\n   342→\n   343→---\n   344→\n   345→# Two-Level Phase Model\n   346→\n   347→The pipeline has 4 top-level **phases**, each containing multiple **workflows** with review loops:\n   348→\n   349→```\n   350→Phase 1: Init\n   351→  └── (inline — no sub-workflows)\n   352→\n   353→Phase 2: Clarifier\n   354→  ├── discover (research) ← research-review loop\n   355→  ├── clarify ← clarification-review loop\n   356→  ├── specify ← spec-challenge loop\n   357→  ├── author (adaptive) ← approval gate\n   358→  ├── design ← design-review loop\n   359→  └── plan ← plan-review loop\n   360→\n   361→Phase 3: Executor\n   362→  ├── execute (per-task) ← task-review loop per task\n   363→  └── verify\n   364→\n   365→Phase 4: Final Review\n   366→  ├── review (final) ← scored review\n   367→  ├── learn\n   368→  └── prepare_next\n   369→```\n   370→\n   371→**Event capture uses both levels.** When emitting phase events, include `--parent-phase`:\n   372→```bash\n   373→wazir capture event --run <id> --event phase_enter --phase discover --parent-phase clarifier --status in_progress\n   374→```\n   375→\n   376→**Progress markers between workflows:** After each workflow completes, output:\n   377→> Phase 2: Clarifier > Workflow: specify (3 of 6 workflows complete)\n   378→\n   379→**`wazir status` shows both levels:** \"Phase 2: Clarifier > Workflow: specify\"\n   380→\n   381→---\n   382→\n   383→# Phase 2: Clarifier\n   384→\n   385→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   386→\n   387→> **Clarifier Phase** — About to research your codebase, clarify requirements, harden the spec, brainstorm designs, and produce an execution plan.\n   388→>\n   389→> **Why this matters:** Without this, I'd guess your tech stack, misunderstand constraints, miss edge cases in the spec, and build the wrong architecture. Every ambiguity left unresolved here becomes a bug or rework cycle later.\n   390→>\n   391→> **Looking for:** Unstated assumptions, scope boundaries, conflicting requirements, missing acceptance criteria\n   392→\n   393→```bash\n   394→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_enter --phase clarifier --status in_progress\n   395→```\n   396→\n   397→Invoke the `wz:clarifier` skill. It handles all sub-workflows internally:\n   398→\n   399→1. **Source Capture** — fetch URLs from input\n   400→2. **Research** (discover workflow) — codebase + external research\n   401→3. **Clarify** (clarify workflow) — scope, constraints, assumptions\n   402→4. **Spec Harden** (specify + spec-challenge workflows) — measurable spec\n   403→5. **Brainstorm** (design + design-review workflows) — design approaches\n   404→6. **Plan** (plan + plan-review workflows) — execution plan\n   405→\n   406→Each sub-workflow has its own review loop. User checkpoints between major steps.\n   407→\n   408→### Scope Invariant\n   409→\n   410→**Hard rule:** `items_in_plan >= items_in_input` unless the user explicitly approves scope reduction. The clarifier MUST NOT autonomously tier, defer, or drop items from the user's input. It can suggest prioritization, but the decision belongs to the user.\n   411→\n   412→Output: approved spec + design + execution plan in `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/`.\n   413→\n   414→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   415→\n   416→> **Clarifier Phase complete.**\n   417→>\n   418→> **Found:** [N] ambiguities resolved, [N] assumptions made explicit, [N] scope boundaries drawn, [N] acceptance criteria hardened\n   419→>\n   420→> **Without this phase:** Requirements would be interpreted differently across tasks, acceptance criteria would be vague and untestable, the design would be ad-hoc, and the plan would miss dependency ordering\n   421→>\n   422→> **Changed because of this work:** [List spec tightening changes, resolved questions, design decisions, scope adjustments]\n   423→\n   424→```bash\n   425→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_exit --phase clarifier --status completed\n   426→```\n   427→\n   428→Run the phase report and display savings to the user:\n   429→```bash\n   430→wazir report phase --run <run-id> --phase clarifier\n   431→wazir stats --run <run-id>\n   432→```\n   433→\n   434→**Show savings in conversation output:**\n   435→> **Context savings this phase:** Used wazir index for [N] queries and context-mode for [M] commands, saving ~[X] tokens ([Y]% reduction). Without these, this phase would have consumed [A] tokens instead of [B].\n   436→\n   437→Output the report content to the user in the conversation.\n   438→\n   439→---\n   440→\n   441→# Phase 3: Executor\n   442→\n   443→**Before starting this phase, output to the user:**\n   444→\n   445→> **Executor Phase** — About to implement [N] tasks in dependency order with TDD (test-first), per-task code review, and verification before each commit.\n   446→>\n   447→> **Why this matters:** Without this discipline, tests get skipped, edge cases get missed, integration points break silently, and review catches problems too late when they're expensive to fix.\n   448→>\n   449→> **Looking for:** Correct dependency ordering, test coverage for each task, clean per-task review passes, no implementation drift from the approved plan\n   450→\n   451→## Phase Gate (Hard Gate)\n   452→\n   453→Before entering the Executor phase, verify ALL clarifier artifacts exist:\n   454→\n   455→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/clarification.md`\n   456→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/spec-hardened.md`\n   457→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/design.md`\n   458→- [ ] `.wazir/runs/latest/clarified/execution-plan.md`\n   459→\n   460→If ANY file is missing, **STOP**:\n   461→\n   462→> **Cannot enter Executor phase: missing prerequisite artifacts from Clarifier.**\n   463→>\n   464→> Missing: [list missing files]\n   465→>\n   466→> The Clarifier phase must complete before execution can begin. Verdicts: PASS (56+), NEEDS MINOR FIXES (42-55), NEEDS REWORK (28-41), FAIL (0-27).\n   551→\n   552→### 4b: Learn (learner role)\n   553→\n   554→Extract durable learnings from the completed run:\n   555→- Scan all review findings (internal + Codex)\n   556→- Propose learnings to `memory/learnings/proposed/`\n   557→- Findings that recur across 2+ runs → auto-proposed as learnings\n   558→- Learnings require explicit scope tags (roles, stacks, concerns)\n   559→\n   560→**Learn workflow completion guard:** If `workflow_policy.learn.enabled: true` in run config AND no files exist in `memory/learnings/proposed/` matching the current run ID pattern (`run-<current-id>-*.md`): log a warning finding: 'Learn workflow enabled but no proposed learnings written for this run'. This ensures the learn workflow always produces output when enabled.\n   561→\n   562→### 4c: Prepare Next (planner role)\n   563→\n   564→Prepare context and handoff for the next run:\n   565→- Write handoff document\n   566→- Compress/archive unneeded files\n   567→- Record what's left to do\n   568→\n   569→**After completing this phase, output to the user:**\n   570→\n   571→> **Final Review Phase complete.**\n   572→>\n   573→> **Found:** [N] findings across 7 dimensions, [N] blocking issues, [N] warnings, [N] learnings proposed for future runs\n   574→>\n   575→> **Without this phase:** Implementation drift from the original request would ship undetected, untested paths would hide production bugs, and recurring mistakes would never get captured as learnings\n   576→>\n   577→> **Changed because of this work:** [List of findings fixed, score achieved, learnings extracted, handoff prepared]\n   578→\n   579→```bash\n   580→wazir capture event --run <run-id> --event phase_exit --phase final_review --status completed\n   581→```\n   582→\n   583→Run the phase report and display it to the user:\n   584→```bash\n   585→wazir report phase --run <run-id> --phase final_review\n   586→```\n   587→\n   588→Output the report content to the user in the conversation.\n   589→\n   590→---\n   591→\n   592→## Step 5: CHANGELOG + Gitflow Validation (Hard Gates)\n   593→\n   594→Before presenting results:\n   595→\n   596→```bash\n   597→wazir validate changelog --require-entries --base main\n   598→wazir validate commits --base main\n   599→```\n   600→\n   601→Both must pass before PR. Review the findings above.\n   651→\n   652→### Run Summary\n   653→\n   654→```bash\n   655→wazir capture summary --run <run-id>\n   656→wazir status --run <run-id> --json\n   657→```\n   658→\n   659→## Error Handling\n   660→\n   661→If any phase fails:\n   662→\n   663→> **Phase [name] failed: [reason]**\n   664→\n   665→Ask the user via AskUserQuestion:\n   666→- **Question:** \"Phase [name] failed: [reason]. Counterfactuals appear in BOTH conversation output AND reasoning files.\n   747→\n   748→## Interaction Rules\n   749→\n   750→- **One question at a time** — never combine multiple questions\n   751→- **Numbered options** — always present choices as numbered lists\n   752→- **Mark defaults** — always show \"(Recommended)\" on the suggested option\n   753→- **Wait for answer** — never proceed past a question until the user responds\n   754→- **No open-ended questions** — every question has concrete options to pick from\n   755→- **Inline answers accepted** — users can type the number or the option name\n   756→"}]},"uuid":"6738f03b-76b1-4aad-8406-4bdb87c3237a","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:35:10.562Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"ce7d207a-4067-40e4-8dfb-f44a55898a6d","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}
